CC   -!- FUNCTION: Recombinant metalloproteinase Mt-d: hydrolyzes
CC       fibronectin, but has no effect on type I gelatin and type I to V
CC       collagens. Selectively hydrolyzes the Aalpha-chain of fibrinogen
CC       (FGA), but has no effect on fibrin.
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Disintegrin: inhibits ADP-induced platelet aggregation
CC       (By similarity).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Recombinant metalloproteinase-disintegrin Mt-d-I (393-
CC       408): hydrolyzes type I gelatin, type III and V collagens, but has
CC       no effect on type I, II, IV collagens and fibronectin. Selectively
CC       hydrolyzes the Aalpha-chain of fibrinogen, but has no effect on
CC       fibrin. May induce hemorrhage in vascular tissue. Strongly
CC       inhibits ADP-induced platelet aggregation. When concentrated, Mt-
CC       d-I undergoes autoproteolytic processing into metalloproteinase
CC       and disintegrin.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 zinc ion per subunit (By similarity).
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ion per subunit (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer; disulfide-linked (disintegrin) (By
CC       similarity).
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted (By similarity).
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the venom metalloproteinase (M12B) family.
CC       P-II subfamily.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 disintegrin domain.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 peptidase M12B domain.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Inhibits fibrinogen interaction with platelets by
CC       binding to the glycoprotein IIb-IIIa receptor. Also inhibits ADP-
CC       induced platelet aggregation. Inhibits basic fibroblast growth
CC       factor (bFGF)-induced proliferation of human vascular endothelial
CC       cell (HUVEC), and vitronectin-induced migration of smooth muscle
CC       cells (SMC). It also regulates platelet activation associated with
CC       HUVEC migration and invasion, suppresses TNF-alpha-induced ovarian
CC       cancer cell proliferation and invasion, and inhibits angiogenesis
CC       and tumor progression.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=7712; Method=MALDI; Range=1-73;
CC       Source=PubMed:11864711;
CC   -!- TOXIC DOSE: LD(50) is 400 mg/kg body weight in male mice and 600
CC       mg/kg in female mice (intravenous). From the autopsies of test
CC       mice, hepatic congestion is found in dead mice, but the organs of
CC       surviving mice lacked any other abnormal indications.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the disintegrin family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 disintegrin domain.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Thrombin-like snake venom protein that release
CC       fibrinopeptide A from fibrinogen (FGA). Shows both kinin-releasing
CC       and coagulant activities.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Selective cleavage of Arg-|-Xaa bond in
CC       fibrinogen, to form fibrin, and release fibrinopeptide A. The
CC       specificity of further degradation of fibrinogen varies with
CC       species origin of the enzyme.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated: contains mannose, galactose, N-
CC       acetylglucosamine, and fucose.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the peptidase S1 family. Snake venom
CC       subfamily.

RP   REVIEW, AND FUNCTION.
RX   PubMed=20186872; DOI=10.1002/cbf.1637;
RA   Dhananjaya B.L., D'Souza C.J.;
RT   "The pharmacological role of nucleotidases in snake venoms.";
RL   Cell Biochem. Funct. 28:171-177(2010).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Hydrolyzes nucleotides into nucleosides (By similarity).
CC       Snake venom 5'-nucleotidases are widely distributed among venomous
CC       snake taxa, but there is a lack of information about their
CC       biological activities. They have been shown to inhibit platelet
CC       aggregation. This effect may be due to the liberation of
CC       inhibitory AMP or adenosine by its action on ADP released upon
CC       initiation of aggregation. Venom 5'-nucleotidases are also known
CC       to synergistically act in vivo with other toxins like ADPases,
CC       phospholipases, and disintegrins to exert a more pronounced anti-
CC       coagulant effect.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: A 5'-ribonucleotide + H(2)O = a ribonucleoside
CC       + phosphate.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake venom serine protease that activates plasminogen.
CC       Weakly hydrolyzes the alpha chain of human fibrinogen without
CC       releasing fibrinopeptide A. Does not hydrolyze plasma kallikrein
CC       or factor Xa. Does not clot fibrinogen. Does not affect platelet
CC       function. Induces hypotensive effects on rats.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Preferential cleavage: Lys-|-Xaa over Arg-|-
CC       Xaa.
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Inhibited by the serine protease inhibitors
CC       NPGB, PMSF, p-aminobenzamidine and aprotinin. Not inhibited by
CC       soybean trypsin inhibitor or EDTA.
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=174 uM for H-D-Val-Leu-Arg-pNA (S-2266);
CC         KM=131 uM for H-D-Val-Leu-Lys-pNA (S-2251);
CC         KM=67 uM for N-p-Tos-Gly-Pro-Lys-pNA;
CC         KM=231 uM for H-D-Pro-Phe-Arg-pNA (S-2302);
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated. PubMed:17034951 shows that it contains
CC       approximately 10% carbohydrates, PubMed:10871053 shows that it
CC       contains approximately 20% carbohydrates.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the peptidase S1 family. Snake venom
CC       subfamily.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 peptidase S1 domain.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalytic subunit of blood coagulation factor X-
CC       activating enzyme. Activates coagulation factor X (F10) by
CC       cleaving the Arg-Ile bond and is also able to activate coagulation
CC       factor IX (F9) and protein S (PROS1) by specific cleavage of Arg-
CC       Ile and Arg-Val bonds.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Specifically activates several components of
CC       the blood clotting system, including coagulation factor X,
CC       coagulation factor IX and protein C by cleavage of Arg-|-Xaa
CC       bonds. Has no action on insulin B chain.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 2 calcium ion per subunit.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 zinc ion per subunit.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterotrimer; disulfide-linked. The heterotrimer consists
CC       of 1 heavy chain and 2 light chains: LC1 and LC2.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated; probably required for conformation. Removal
CC       of easily accessible sugars does not change its functional
CC       capacity, but removal of the core sugars with N-glycanase causes a
CC       virtually complete loss of enzyme activity, apparently as a result
CC       of major conformational changes in the molecule. Not O-
CC       glycosylated.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the venom metalloproteinase (M12B) family.
CC       P-III subfamily. P-IIId sub-subfamily.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 disintegrin domain.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 peptidase M12B domain.

RP   FUNCTION ON MELANOMA CELLS.
RX   PubMed=17854854; DOI=10.1016/j.toxicon.2007.07.016;
RA   Oliva I.B., Coelho R.M., Barcellos G.G., Saldanha-Gama R.,
RA   Wermelinger L.S., Marcinkiewicz C., Zingali R.B., Barja-Fidalgo C.;

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Binds alpha-5/beta-1 (ITGAV/ITGB1), alpha-v/beta-3
CC       (ITGAV/ITGB3) and alpha-M/beta-2 (ITGAM/ITGB2) integrins. Is a
CC       potent inhibitor of platelet aggregation induced by ADP, collagen,
CC       and thrombin. Induces neutrophil chemotaxis and inhibits the
CC       chemotaxis of human neutrophils toward fMLP, IL-8, and jarastatin
CC       itself. Directly activates an integrin-coupled signaling and
CC       modulate the MAPK pathway in different ways, leading the
CC       neutrophils to express different functional response. Jarastatin-
CC       treated neutrophils accumulates F-actin at the plasmalemma.
CC       Induces PTK2/FAK1 and phosphoinositide 3-kinase (PI3K) activation.
CC       Induces Erk-2 translocation to nucleus and a delay of the
CC       spontaneous apoptosis of neutrophils. Increases the IL-8 mRNA
CC       levels in neutrophils. When injected simultaneously with melanoma
CC       cells in mice, jarastatin, flavoridin (FL) and kistrin (KR),
CC       significantly reduce tumor lung colonization. Jarastatin inhibits
CC       B16F10 cell growth in vitro. When it interacts with melanoma
CC       cells, it induces actin cytoskeleton rearrangement, increasing
CC       actin polymerization and PTK2/FAK1 phosphorylation. Interferes
CC       with NF-kappaB translocation in melanoma cells.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MASS SPECTROMETRY: Mass=7753.89; Method=MALDI; Range=16-88;
CC       Source=PubMed:16919699;
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the disintegrin family.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 disintegrin domain.

RP   GLYCOSYLATION.
RC   TISSUE=Venom;
RX   PubMed=17963685; DOI=10.1016/j.abb.2007.10.002;
RA   Sanchez E.F., Gabriel L.M., Gontijo S., Gremski L.H., Veiga S.S.,
RA   Evangelista K.S., Eble J.A., Richardson M.;
RT   "Structural and functional characterization of a P-III
RT   metalloproteinase, leucurolysin-B, from Bothrops leucurus venom.";
RL   Arch. Biochem. Biophys. 468:193-204(2007).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake venom zinc metalloproteinase that acts as a potent
CC       hemorrhagic toxin. Hydrolyzes the insulin B chain at the 14-Ala-|-
CC       Leu-15 bond but not the 16-Tyr-|-Leu-17 bond. Degrades the alpha-
CC       chain of fibrin and hydrolyzes the Aalpha-chain of fibrinogen
CC       (FGA) while leaving the beta and gamma chains unaffected. Degrades
CC       type-I collagen and its gelatin. Degrades the alpha-1 chain of
CC       type-IV collagen and its gelatin but not the alpha-2 chain.
CC       Degrades plasma fibronectin, plasma vitronectin and basement
CC       membrane enactin. It inhibits collagen-induced platelet
CC       aggregation but does not interact with alpha-1/beta-1 or alpha-
CC       2/beta-1 integrin.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 zinc ion per subunit (By similarity).
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Binds 1 calcium ions per subunit (By similarity).
CC   -!- ENZYME REGULATION: Inhibited by EDTA, but not by PMSF. Pre-
CC       incubation with 2 mM DTT completely abolishes activity.
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       pH dependence:
CC         Optimum pH is 7.5-9.3 with dimethyl casein as substrate;
CC       Temperature dependence:
CC         Optimum temperature is 30 degrees Celsius with dimethyl casein
CC         as substrate;
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated.
CC   -!- PTM: The N-terminus is blocked (Probable).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the venom metalloproteinase (M12B) family.
CC       P-III subfamily.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 disintegrin domain.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 peptidase M12B domain.

RT   "The pharmacological role of nucleotidases in snake venoms.";
RL   Cell Biochem. Funct. 28:171-177(2010).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Hydrolyzes nucleotides into nucleosides (By similarity).
CC       Snake venom 5'-nucleotidases are widely distributed among venomous
CC       snake taxa, but there is a lack of information about their
CC       biological activities. They have been shown to inhibit platelet
CC       aggregation. This effect may be due to the liberation of
CC       inhibitory AMP or adenosine by its action on ADP released upon
CC       initiation of aggregation. Venom 5'-nucleotidases are also known
CC       to synergistically act in vivo with other toxins like ADPases,
CC       phospholipases, and disintegrins to exert a more pronounced anti-
CC       coagulant effect.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: A 5'-ribonucleotide + H(2)O = a ribonucleoside
CC       + phosphate.
CC   -!- COFACTOR: Zinc (By similarity).
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Trimer or tetramer (Probable).
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane (By similarity); Lipid-anchor, GPI-
CC       anchor (By similarity).
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- PTM: Venom 5'-nucleotidases (or a part thereof) may be released
CC       into the venom via exosome-like vesicles. They may be attached via
CC       a GPI anchor to the membrane of these vesicles. Soluble forms of
CC       5'-nucleotidase might be released by cleavage of the ectodomain in
CC       the exosome-like vesicles or venom gland cells.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the 5'-nucleotidase family.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Snake venom serine protease with strong beta-
CC       fibrinogenolytic activities, angiotensin I (AGT)-degrading
CC       activities and strong kallikrein-like activities in vitro,
CC       releasing bradykinin from kininogen (KNG1). Intravenous injection
CC       mildly lowers blood pressure in experimental rats, which may be
CC       explained by the action on angiotensin I and kininogen.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Exhibits amidase activity against N-benzoyl-
CC       Pro-Phe-Arg-p-nitroanilide.
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Temperature dependence:
CC         Heat-stable to about 95 degrees Celsius;
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Monomer.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Expressed by the venom gland.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Does not have activity on gamma-chains of
CC       fibrinogen (FGG) (PubMed:7811255), and does not coagulate human
CC       plasma. Does not induce or inhibit platelet aggregation
CC       (PubMed:11237764).
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the peptidase S1 family. Snake venom
CC       subfamily.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 peptidase S1 domain.
CC   -!- CAUTION: The correspondance between the sequence (indicated in
CC       PubMed:7811255) and the function (from PubMed:11237764) has not
CC       been clearly demonstrated.
